[HEADING] 4. Maintenance of Supplemental Services

[HEADING] a. Current Provision and Plans for Continued Services

[TEXT] Expanded Cancer Screening: FPCSN was awarded Accelerating Cancer Screening (AxCS) funding in 2024 to increase colorectal cancer screening and referral in collaboration with the Spectrum FQHC, the Philadelphia Health Federation and its HCCN, and the Penn Abramson Cancer Center. The partnering organizations are focusing on the unscreened patient population of the participating health centers, comprising approximately five thousand residents of Philadelphia, who are predominantly low-income, African American, and experience multiple barriers to health care services. Through centralized use of population health management systems, the project team developed outreach lists for mailings that include patient education and a FIT kit, thus enabling a broad, efficient approach to addressing gaps in preventive screening. Text messages informed by behavioral science encourage patients to use the FIT kits and mail back their tests. The health centers' systems are being used to track and follow-up on results. The Cancer Center supports the health centers with expertise in mailed FIT campaigns as well as through a contracted Navigator who provides intensive, personalized services to patients who have a positive FIT and need colonoscopy and possible follow-up care. Through this methodology, the partnering organizations expect to double rates of colorectal cancer screening. The project is testing the viability of centralized, technology-enabled outreach for cancer screening, in order to support enhanced capacity for navigation services in FQHCs.

[TEXT] b. New Applicant Plan to Ensure Access to Health Center Program-Funded Programming As noted above, the health center has been providing health care services in the service area for 33 years. Because the previous awardee changed ownership and relinquished the grant on 6/30/25, the FPCSN health center has had to establish a new non-profit corporation and apply as a new applicant for the area it has served for many years. This SAC application is being submitted to ensure that patients continue to have access to the services FPCSN provides, including those the Health Center Program has provided funding in the past to establish or expand. FPCSN has gathered tremendous support from the community. FPCSN has been able to keep all main and sites and the school sites open while providing all required services. Understanding it will be some time before the health center again has FQHC status and supports, the Penn hospital system, a major health-focused foundation, the area insurers, PACHC and the Health Fed, local civic leaders, and the state are all supporting and assisting the health center through this period in order to maintain FPCSN services and support our patients.

[HEADING] 5. Sliding Fee Discount Program

[HEADING] a. Sliding Fee Assessment

[TEXT] FPCSN policy, approved by the Board, is that all required primary, preventive, dental, behavioral health, and additional health services are available and accessible to the target population without regard to patients' ability to pay, and that the health center has a sliding fee discount scale geared to U.S. poverty guidelines. Procedures dictate screening is conducted to determine all patients' eligibility for services under the sliding scale during the initial intake and annually. FPCSN ensures that patients are made aware of the sliding fee discount program by providing information on the website, signs in each site, and notifying patients during appointment scheduling and registration. To assess their eligibility for discounted fees, patients are asked to provide their family size and income information. Patients applying for the sliding fee scale discount program must present income documentation to determine income level that includes: previous year's tax return, current pay stub, pension check stub, beneficiary award

[TEXT] 23



========== PAGE 34 (from PDF footer) ==========

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242645

[TEXT] Grant Number: N/A

[HEADING] Family Practice & Counseling Services Network 2026 Service Area Competition Application

[TEXT] letter (Social Security benefits, etc.), or personal attestation of earnings for people with no tax liability and/or who are self-employed. If patients do not have proper documentation with them, they are provided time to provide it for the discount to be applied to the visit. Once a discount has been approved, it is honored for a year, when the patient must reapply. Patients have the right to refuse to complete the assessment; they will be ineligible for discounts.

[HEADING] b. How Patient Charges are Adjusted Based on Ability to Pay

[TEXT] FPCN has sliding fee scales for Primary Care, Behavioral Health, Integrated Behavioral Health, and Dental services. The FPCSN sliding scales are revised annually and approved by the Board, include three categories between 100% and 200% of federal poverty level, and are used for all clinical services. (See the sliding scale in Attachment 10) The scales and procedures are on hand for staff who register patients and they receive training in how charges are adjusted according to health center policy. The scales are embedded within the EHR to automatically calculate the discounts once family size and income are entered. Attempts are made to collect discounted fees, but patients are not refused care as a result of non-payment. Hence, no one is denied services due to their inability to pay.

[TEXT] c Sliding Fee Schedule Structure and Nominal Fees

[TEXT] There are $20 nominal charges in place for patients with income below 100% of poverty for primary care services, which can be waived in some cases. These nominal charges are flat charges, they are not set at the actual cost of the service provided, and they are set at a level that is nominal from the perspective of the patient.

[HEADING] d. Evaluation of Sliding Fee Discount Program

[TEXT] FPCSN policy requires that the Board reviews, revises as needed, and approves the policy and supporting operating procedures, including the schedule of charges, and those regarding the billing and collections of patient accounts, on an annual basis. This review is designed to determine that, from the perspective of the patient, the sliding fee scales do not create barriers to service. The Board uses patient satisfaction surveys for this evaluation and seeks input from patient members on the Board and from the Community Advisory Committees regarding potential barriers the fees might pose for patients.

[HEADING] 6. Care that is Respectful of and Responsive to Individual Needs

[TEXT] a/b. Engagement of Patients in Care and Involvement with Families and Caregivers FPCSN services aim to improve patients' quality of life as defined by the individuals or families being served. Including families and caregivers in care, if the patient consents, is shown to increase health outcomes not only for patients but for families as well. It is critical that families are involved when appropriate to assist in strengthening the family unit through the services we provide. Goals for physical health, behavioral health, and meeting health related social needs are set with the patient and family, with a focus on what is important to them. Through discussion, providers and staff assure they fully understand the treatment options available and then that they understand details of the treatment regimen that is decided upon. If there are health-related social barriers to patients' receiving or implementing their treatment, such as needing to travel to a specialist, connect with food as medicine, or participate in exercise, referrals are made to assist patients with these needs. In some cases, behavioral health services are needed to help overcome barriers as well. Providers and all other staff have received training that helps them to be sensitive to the difficulties many patients have experienced that affect their ability to connect to services.

[HEADING] c. Alignment with the Needs of the Underserved Area Population

[TEXT] Since its inception over 30 years ago, the health center has been focused on increasing high quality integrated health care for those residents of the service area who are underserved as a result of their low-income status. FPCSN uses a number of ways to be sure that services are aligned with the needs of the communities served across Northwest, North, and Southwest Philadelphia and nearby Delaware County, areas experiencing high poverty, chronic disease, and limited access to care. Serving more than 15,000 patients annually, FPCSN provides comprehensive, integrated services including primary care, behavioral health, dental, perinatal, and enabling services that address social determinants of health.

[TEXT] Formal needs assessments are done at least every three years, as well as when a new service or site is proposed either internally or by an external partner such as the Housing Authority, the PHA Tenants' Council, or the School District. Guided by its Strategic Plan and CQI framework, FPCSN uses population data, UDS metrics, and health screenings to identify gaps in care and target resources. FPCSN's Board of Directors, which includes community representatives, reviews outcome data to ensure operations remain responsive and equitable. There are a majority of patient members on the Board who provide valuable information about how the health center is doing in serving the community and each site has a Community Advisory Committee that helps the director and staff to keep in touch with community residents and partners and their ongoing needs. Through these coordinated strategies, FPCSN advances principles of accessibility and focus on community needs, ensuring all patients, regardless of income or background, receive high-quality and responsive care.

[HEADING] 7. Process for Continuity of Care

[HEADING] a. Communication Tools

[TEXT] FPCSN is committed to ensuring that information on patient hospitalizations, including emergency department visits, is obtained and reviewed in a timely manner. The health center is part of the HealthShare Exchange (HSX) that provides the health center with real-time notice about health center patients who have been admitted to and discharged from participating hospitals for inpatient stays and emergency department visits. Staff have access to visit summaries that include prescription information and testing results, as well as the discharge summaries of FPCSN patients through area health systems electronic records. The health center works with area hospitals and other health providers in an integrated model of care, in that there are HIPAA-compliant arrangements for these providers to directly access the FPCSN EHR. Through the EHR, FPCSN staff receive information from the hospitals including lab and diagnostic results, and emergency care notes. Also, through the Azara population health management tool and the Aledade Accountable Care Organization FPCSN is a part of, the health center receives notifications of hospital and ER utilization that the Care Coordinators manage.

[HEADING] b. Hospital Admitting

[TEXT] FPCSN works with the hospitals in the service area to assure patients referred by the health center will be admitted. All of the hospitals offer emergency and diagnostic care and a broad range of medical specialties and services and most are teaching hospitals that have affiliations with local universities. A formal agreement is in place with the Hospital of the University of Pennsylvania for referred patients to be admitted and have their care managed by hospitalists. Obstetric patients are accepted for inpatient delivery as part of the contracts in place with the Family Medicine group whose contract providers attend those patients and conduct medical rounds. These arrangements

[TEXT] 25



========== PAGE 36 (from PDF footer) ==========

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242645

[TEXT] Grant Number: N/A

[HEADING] Family Practice & Counseling Services Network 2026 Service Area Competition Application

[TEXT] include an integrated model of care, in that the prenatal providers can access the FPCSN EHR for any needed information when a mother presents for delivery and delivery information, including the birthweight, is input directly in the patient's FPCSN chart. In all cases, information about patients' treatment and needs upon discharge is communicated to health center staff.

[TEXT] c. Receipt, Follow-up, Recording of Medical Information from Referral Sources

[TEXT] FPCSN staff receive information from the hospitals when patients visit the emergency department or are hospitalized directly into the EHR via the HSX HealthShare Exchange and via fax from the payers. Summaries are imported directly into the patient's chart by the Exchange and medications lists are updated. Staff then have access to visit summaries that include prescription information and testing results, as well as the discharge summaries of these FPCSN patients.

[HEADING] d. Health Center Follow-up for Hospitalizations or ED Visits

[TEXT] Most of the area hospitals send lab and diagnostic results, as well as emergency care notes, directly into the EHR. When patients are scheduled for discharge, they are given instructions regarding their medications, limitations on physical activity, and dates for follow-up care at the FPCSN and health center care management staff is notified electronically so that transition to outpatient care can be facilitated. An FPCSN care coordinator at each site follows up on all patients who have had emergency room visits or hospitalizations to ensure there is a follow up plan in place to see their FPCSN provider or a specialist, that they understand and are taking their medication, and that they have a support system in place from family or community nursing services. Social service staff makes referrals as needed to a variety of community services, such as in-home services and Meals-on-Wheels, to provide that support for patients in the community.

[HEADING] 8. New Applicant Plan to Limit Disruption

[TEXT] As noted above, the health center has been providing health care services in the service area for 33 years. Because the previous awardee changed ownership and relinquished the grant on 6/30/25, the FPCSN health center has had to establish a new non-profit corporation and apply as a new applicant for the area it has served for many years. FPCSN has been able to keep all main sites open while providing all required services in order to limit disruption and this SAC application is being submitted to ensure that patients continue to have access to the services FPCSN provides. FPCSN has gathered tremendous support from the community. Understanding it will be some time before the health center again has FQHC status and supports, the Penn hospital system, a major health-focused foundation, the area insurers, and the state are all supporting and assisting the health center through this period in order to maintain FPCSN services and support our patients.

[HEADING] 4. Applicants requesting PHPC Funding

[TEXT] a/b. How Public Housing Residents Are Involved in Planning and Ongoing Administration The FPCSN health centers have been created in partnership with the communities they serve and their services are reflective of community need and in partnership with the Philadelphia Housing Authority. The collaborative relationship with the Housing Authority has continued through the 33 years the FPCSN has been providing health services to public housing residents. The Network began in the Abbottsford Homes, a tenant-managed community, where the health center has always had a strong relationship with tenant leadership based on mutual respect. A resident of Abbottsford Homes was the President of the health center advisory committee for 26 years. The FPCSN Board members include one member who is a representative of the Housing Authority and two others who are or have been public housing residents.

[TEXT] As noted above, each of the comprehensive FPCSN sites now has a Community Advisory Committee to help the site understand the needs and opinions of the community. The Network Community Engagement Manager facilitates Community Advisory Committee meetings at each site that include patients, including current and former PHA residents, recruited in partnership with PHA Tenant Councils, to ensure diverse community representation. She also leads quarterly patient town halls, creating an efficient communication platform where patients discuss new initiatives, service quality, and emerging needs. Insights from these meetings directly inform programming, outreach, and CQI priorities, as does the Strategic Plan. Through these coordinated strategies, FPCSN stays closely aligned with the needs of residents in Philadelphia Housing Authority communities through a coordinated model of care and community engagement. Through these structures, FPCSN integrates resident feedback into program design, resulting in initiatives like patient access, health education and outreach, perinatal wellness, and food security programs. This collaborative approach ensures that FPCSN services remain responsive, community-led, and aligned with the lived experiences of public housing residents.

[HEADING] CAPACITY 1. Organizational Structure

[TEXT] Family Practice & Counseling Services Network, Inc. is a 501(c)3 organization registered in Pennsylvania and listed with the IRS. The structure, management system, and lines of authority are appropriate to the delivery of high-quality care and are fully compliant with Section 330 requirements. As noted on the Organization Chart and Bylaws (Attachments 2 and 3), the organization is governed by a Board of Directors that elects its own members and exists to operate the FPCSN health center. The Board hires and evaluates the Executive Director/CEO. FPCSN has an Executive Team, Senior Leadership Team and Extended Leadership team that manage all aspects of the health center operations.

[HEADING] b/c. Subawards and Contractors

[HEADING] 2. Management/Executive Team

[TEXT] FPCSN has a very experienced Executive Team and the expertise and capabilities to manage the operation and oversight of the health center. All of the managers, including the CEO who is the Project Director, are hired directly. The FPCSN Chief Executive Officer reports to the Board and has responsibility for day-to-day operations, working with the Executive Leadership Team, which meets formally each week and includes the Chief Operations Officer (COO), the Chief Finance Officer (CFO), the Chief Clinical Officer (CD) , the Chief Compliance Officer, the Chief Strategy and Development Officer, and the Chief Human Resources Officer. A Senior Leadership Team that meets bi-weekly also includes the clinical directors for behavioral health, integrated behavioral health, and oral health, and the directors of the sites, and the Chief IT Officer (CIO).

[TEXT] Emily Nichols has been the Executive Director of the health center since 2019. She was Director of Operations for six years and Director of one of the sites for three years before that. Her career has focused on Philadelphia-based FQHCs in a variety of roles centering on patient care, health outcomes, quality improvement, and patient-centered medical home recognition. She holds a BA in Public Health/Social and Behavioral Sciences from Johns Hopkins University and an MPH from Emory University with a concentration in Behavioral Sciences. Emily is dedicated to quality programming driven by population need and strives for outcomes that meet those needs in addressing the health-related social needs that can prevent engagement in health care services.

[TEXT] Aaron Chavis is the FPCSN Chief Operations Officer. He holds a BA in Law and Justice from Rowan University and a Master of Public Administration from Florida State University and he has worked in the capacity of Interim Executive Director and Vice President of Operations over his career. Aaron manages FPCSN operations with the Center Directors and over 150 employees to ensure all programming is uniform and in keeping with the agency's principals and mission. The position of Chief Clinical Officer is vacant and the Clinical Director position is being filled on an interim basis by Jennifer Cohn, MD, from the Penn Department of Family Medicine and Community Health. She has provided obstetric and collaborative physician services for FPCSN for a number of years. The Chief Financial Officer position is held by Marcus Freeman who is a seasoned healthcare executive with more than twenty years of leadership experience within FQHCs and community-based healthcare organizations. The Chief Information Officer is Cheryl Rodenfels, who is also a consultant. She brings almost 20 years of IT service management and leadership, much of it in healthcare organizations.

[TEXT] The FPCSN Executive and Leadership Teams provide robust support for the operation and oversight of the health center and all of its programs by establishing a framework for policy implementation, accountability, and risk management. Regular supervision occurs for all staff with regular team meetings. To ensure accountability, the health center management uses the

[HEADING] b. Promotion of Innovation and Quality Improvement

[TEXT] The FPCSN Executive Team promotes innovation and a culture of quality improvement and has worked to improve patient satisfaction, make technology enhancements to increase access to care, review staff compensation packages to be competitive and support staff retention, and enhance financial sustainability through added services and other funding opportunities. The team actively engages with the community to identify needs and develop responsive solutions, in particular through partnership with PACHC and the Health Federation and its HCCN. This engagement is also achieved through regular community needs assessments, patient satisfaction surveys, and staff feedback mechanisms. At FPCSN, innovations most often come from clinicians or other staff and they are always focused on improving the quality of health or life for patients and the community served. The Executive Team works with the Quality Improvement Committee that is tasked with analyzing data, piloting revised care models, and implementing evidence-based practices. Innovation has been fostered by allocating resources for pilot projects and encouraging an innovation mentality, where lessons learned from unsuccessful initiatives are used to inform future efforts. By creating an environment where feedback is valued and new ideas are encouraged, the Executive Team works to ensure the health center remains adaptable, effective, and truly responsive to the evolving needs of the community it serves.

[TEXT] The FPCSN Strategic Plan and Continuous Quality Improvement Plan promote innovation and continuous quality improvement in the organization. These frameworks guide organizational priorities, align quality goals with community needs, and ensure evidence-based decision-making across all departments. Accountability for quality and innovation is embedded at every level. The FPCSN Board of Directors provides governance and oversees strategic direction and outcomes; the Executive Leadership Team provides strategic direction and ensures alignment throughout the Network; and the Senior Leadership Team (Department Leaders) manages implementation of performance and quality initiatives. The Extended Leadership Team that includes leaders across all FPCSN sites, meets monthly to review Network data, progress, and operational improvements. The CQI Committee meets quarterly to evaluate outcomes, monitor metrics, and update the CQI Plan. FPCSN's CQI process integrates patient feedback, survey data, and Community Advisory Committee input to inform service enhancements and pilot innovative care models. This structured, data-driven approach fosters accountability, transparency, and cross- departmental collaboration, ensuring innovation and quality remain central to achieving equitable, high-performing, and patient-centered care.

[HEADING] 3. Recruitment and Retention of Qualified Providers

[TEXT] When recruitment for management or provider positions is necessary, FPCSN uses all available avenues and tools to find the most qualified people and people who are motivated to work with the underserved patients and communities FPCSN serves. The health center assures that potential candidates are aware of the advantages of working for the Network, including the mentoring they will receive from the experienced leadership and providers, the opportunities they will have to

These activities ensure staff are as involved as possible in health center operations and decision-making to maximize their investment in the program and the work they and their colleagues are doing. FPCSN has had a recent initiative around the prevention of burn out and promotion of self-care, through which Mind-Body staff are available to staff as well as patients.

[HEADING] 4. Financial Accounting and Control Systems

[TEXT] In order to maintain its high degree of financial accuracy, FPCSN employs a solid financial management system. To assure that Generally Accepted Accounting Principles are followed, exacting internal controls are utilized, in that: 1) fiscal procedures are developed, continually updated, and stringently followed; 2) budgets are properly developed, approved, reviewed, and managed by a fiscal team; 3) all financial transactions are properly recorded and fully disclosed to all relevant parties; 4) all administrative costs are properly documented and periodically reviewed for their accuracy; 5) a professional audit of all fiscal matters is performed annually by a recognized outside auditing firm and reviewed by the FPCSN Board of Directors.

[HEADING] a. Control Over Health Center Funds

[TEXT] The FPCSN Chief Financial Officer acts to ensure that the activities of the health center are managed appropriately, run as efficiently as possible, are staffed appropriately, and ensure that GAAP standards can be maintained and FPCSN policies and procedures are followed. When necessary, the CFO recommends the need for policy and/or procedure change when that change enhances the efficiency of the department. The CFO works to ensure that the Financial Policies and Procedures meet all Federal, State, Government and Private guidelines, including federal payment management system requirements. This includes policies and procedures as they relate to grant funding as well as third party billing. FPCSN Policies specifically address IRS Filing, Audit, Insurance Coverage, Procurement, Internal Controls, Fee Schedules and Discounts, Billing and Collections, Budget and Accounting, Grants Management and staff travel. Accounting procedures maintain effective control over, and accountability for, all funds, property, and other assets.

[HEADING] b. Tracking of Financial Performance

[TEXT] FPCSN's accounting procedures maintain effective control over, and accountability for, all funds, property, and other assets and are in full compliance with federal, state and local regulations. They include the following specific accounting areas: check requisitions, invoices, accounts payable, accounts receivable, inventory, leases, cash receipts, payroll, benefits, and insurance. There is a comprehensive chart of accounts, ranging from wages and salaries to staff travel to property repair. Separate units have been established for each health center and clinical department, allowing revenue and expenses to be identified and directly charged to related programs. Effective segregation of duties represents a vital component to the organization's

[HEADING] Family Practice & Counseling Services Network 2026 Service Area Competition Application

[TEXT] internal control system. Segregation of duties controls are designed and reviewed as an internal control to help prevent employees from committing errors or engaging in fraudulent activity. The system is under the supervision of the CFO who has long experience in complying with general accounting procedures. The system is sufficient to assure that all health center revenues are used solely for authorized purposes.

[TEXT] FPCSN financial management activities are centralized, computerized, and readily accessible for audit and review. FPCSN utilizes AthenaPractice and VisDental practice management software, which have reports on revenue by source, aged accounts receivable by source, provider productivity, and encounters by payor category, among many other financial reports. In addition, monthly general ledger financial and budget reports allow management to analyze the organization's financial standing and trends. These systems allow FPCSN to enter and process demographic, clinical, and billing data. Patients can be identified by age, gender, zip code, income eligibility, family size, clinical services provided, insurance payer, and other demographics. Both practice management systems allow billed and actual payment to be reconciled. It also provides an accurate aged account receivable given the reimbursement processes of some organization funders. This system is key to many areas of patient billing as a threshold can be selected to initiate a follow-up or action. The system allows denials, cash payment cycles and other key operating indicators to be monitored. FPCSN is able to download billing and account receivable information directly into the current general ledger system to allow the finance department to perform reconciliations in a consistent and timely manner.

[HEADING] c. Accounting for a 330 Award and Other Awards and Funds

[TEXT] The financial accounting and internal control systems assure that all federal and other funds are fully accounted for, including maintaining source documentation, that all expenditures of funds are allowable, which will include Section 330 and other federal awards, and that only actual work performed is charged to each funding source. Funds received are tracked in separate general ledger accounts. Salaries and wages and other non-personnel costs supported by any funds are recorded in these separate general ledger accounts.

[HEADING] d. Mitigation of Conflict of Interest

[TEXT] To assure that decisions are free of bias, interest, or personal benefit or gain on the part of any member of the Board of Directors, Executive Team, or any other staff, FPCSN has a Conflict of Interests Policy, which states that "No Board member, officer, employee, or agent shall participate in FPCSN's selection, award, or administration of any contract or grant when a real or apparent conflict of interest is involved". The policy states that "For purposes of contracting, a 'Conflict of Interest' arises when an employee, officer, director or agent, any member of his, her or their immediate family, his/her/their partner or an organization which employs or is about to employ any of those parties, has a financial, fiduciary or other interest in, and/or derives a tangible personal benefit from a firm considered by FPCSN for a contract". The policy details the process by which conflicts will be determined and the process of recusal when a conflict exists. All Board members and staff must sign a Conflict Reporting Form at least annually confirming any conflicts of interest they may have or their non-conflicting status. The Conflict of Interests Policy is referenced in the FPCSN Procurement Policy that requires that all procurement transactions should be conducted in a manner to provide open and free competition and in the FPCSN Bylaws.

[HEADING] 5. Planning for Disasters and Emergencies

[TEXT] FPCSN has an Emergency Preparedness and Response Plan that outlines the health center's response to a disaster, including ways that patients would continue to receive care; how FPCSN would integrate its response with those of City agencies, area hospitals, and other medical providers; and how health center providers could be deployed to other organizations. An Emergency Response Team includes professional medical staff such as medical assistants, nurses and nurse practitioners, behavioral health staff such as therapists and crisis specialists, and some administrative personnel. The health centers will not be points of distribution for antibiotics, vaccines, and medical supplies; rather, staff will be deployed to city sites to assist in distribution. FPCSN will work with the City to integrate with its preparedness, conducting annual drills in coordination with the city if needed. FPCSN will have a plan for an emergency situation that is coordinated with the City's plan. The health center has insurance to prevent financial revenue and facilities loss in an emergency, as well as downtime procedures for each clinical department to ensure we can provide services in emergency situations. The Pennsylvania Forum for Primary Health Emergency Preparedness Manual, which is extensive, is the basis for the FPCSN Plan.

[HEADING] 6. Factors Affecting Three-Year Trend

[TEXT] The UDS reports filed over the last three years when the health center was operating as an FQHC indicated that the health center served 14,872 patients in CY2022, 15,214 patients in CY2023, and 15,617 patients in CY 2024. So, the trend has been upward since the pandemic. However, in the last twelve months, because of the upheaval and uncertainty of the separation from RHD and loss of FQHC status, many providers and other staff have left to seek positions elsewhere. As a result, further growth in the next year is not being projected in this application but as new staff are hired, FPCSN will increase the number of patients served.

[HEADING] IMPACT/EVALUATIVE MEASURES

[HEADING] 1. Quality Improvement and Quality Assurance Program

[TEXT] The FPCSN quality improvement process is led by a Continuous Quality Improvement Committee that is headed by the Quality Manager and includes the CEO, the Primary Care Director and the Chief Clinical Officer, and the Department Heads from Integrated Behavioral Health, Outpatient Behavioral Health, Dental, Human Resources, and Finance. The CQI Committee is charged with enhancing the organization's performance by setting benchmarks, measuring progress made toward those goals, determining and implementing improvement plans when necessary.

[TEXT] The purview of the CQI Committee includes four areas:

[TEXT]  Oversight and compliance, including policies and protocols, staff credentials, the risk management program, emergency training, and the peer review process;

[TEXT]  Quality Improvement and Quality Assurance, including internal controls and procedures, reports on performance on quality measures, identifying and analyzing areas identified for improvement, support of PDSA (Plan-Do-Study-Act) improvement cycles, and tracking patient and staff satisfaction;

[TEXT]  Pay for Performance, Incentives, and Productivity; and

[TEXT]  Financial Metrics.

[TEXT] The Quality Manager, in partnership with Department Directors, is responsible for assuring that all staff, as well as Board and Site Advisory Committee members, are trained in the CQI process.

[HEADING] a. Follows Clinical Guidelines and Standards of Care

[TEXT] As noted above, FPCSN is recognized as a Patient Centered Medical Home. The health center has extensive operating procedures and clinical protocols in place that further this recognition. Evidence based guidelines and Clinical Decision Support tools are embedded in the electronic medical record, so that providers and staff receive prompts for patient care based on their diagnoses and services they provide. FPCSN has protocols in place regarding the care of obesity, diabetes, hypertension, cardiovascular health and risk reduction, cancer screening, screening for depression and behavioral health, prenatal care, women's health, infant immunization, and asthma. The Azara DRVS and i2iTracks population management software provides data reports regarding providers' adherence to these protocols and the outcomes for their patients in dashboards that include individual practitioner, clinic site, and health center results. These are used in supervision, site and health center management, and in the aggregate by the Board for decision making regarding the health center.

[TEXT] The FPCSN Quality Improvement and Risk Management Procedures indicate the processes to be conducted to maintain and continually improve the quality of care provided by the health centers. The providers conduct audits of each other's charts bi-annually, under the peer review procedure, during which they review practice performance for completeness of charting, accuracy of coding, and documentation of preventive care and activities satisfying quality of care measures as defined by the Network as well as HEDIS measures and other external benchmarks.

[HEADING] b. Addresses Patient Safety

[TEXT] FPCSN has an established incident reporting system whereby personnel are required to bring to the attention of appropriate administrative staff any incident that affects or threatens to affect the health and/or safety of any person associated with the health centers. Procedures exist that detail any external parties that must be notified, such as for suspected child abuse or neglect, and how such notice should occur. Incidents reported are reviewed in the CQI Committee. Adverse incidents are reviewed by the Primary Care Director and the Executive Director, along with other managers and supervisory staff appropriate to the situation. Incidents provide information to be used in revision of processes, training of staff, and other actions that will increase the level of safety for patients and staff. All incidents reported are reviewed quarterly by the CQI committee and are assigned a red, yellow, or green status to indicate the severity of the incident. Sentinel events are incidents that result in harm, injury, or death to a patient or a person associated with the health centers. Sentinel events are investigated by the Primary Care Director and a thorough chart review is conducted with other clinical leaders if the affected person is a patient.

[HEADING] Risk Management

[TEXT] FPCSN has policies and procedures that govern its risk management processes, including those related to facility maintenance and inspections, monitoring of OSHA requirements, incident and accident response and review, fire and emergency drills, confidentiality and HIPAA compliance, and credentialing and privileging procedures. Each site has a written plan for dealing with fire and other life-threatening situations that details evacuation procedures, including how children or persons with disabilities will be assisted. The plans also indicate how management will be notified and the plan of action in case a site must be closed as a result of the crisis. Fire drills are held quarterly in each site, with at least one per year held when regular services for clients are being held. The CQI process monitors these processes and implements any quality improvement projects needed to assure that patients and staff are as safe as possible and that risk is minimized.

[TEXT] FPCSN procedures cover employees' responsibility to notice and report any potential hazards in the health centers. Quarterly inspections are done by the Compliance Manager in each site to detect unsafe conditions, initiate preventive maintenance, and monitor actions on work required. Such inspections cover all aspects of facility safety, including OSHA, Department of Health, Fire Department, and ADA requirements and any other laws and regulations, including those requiring proper signage in the centers. Plumbing, ventilation, heating, cooling, lighting, fire extinguishers, and alarm systems are all included in the inspection process. Any problems discovered during the inspection process are addressed as quickly as possible. Any preventive maintenance needed is also noted and completed. All staff are expected to take all necessary safety precautions when operating health center equipment or securing the premises. Smoking is not permitted in the health centers or when staff are escorting patients or during outreach work.

[HEADING] c. Improves Patient Experience and Satisfaction

[TEXT] The FPCSN QI Plan indicates that annual patient satisfaction surveys will be conducted, but these actually take place much more often. Plans are underway to use the patient portal to conduct brief surveys after every visit. The results of these surveys are reviewed in the CQI Committee, which develops any needed quality improvement projects. The results of the surveys and resulting actions are shared with the site advisory committees, shared with health center staff, and put on the website to assure patients that the surveys are used and their voices are being heard. FPCSN has a Patients' Complaints and Grievances Policy that affirms patients' rights to voice grievances regarding their care, without recrimination, and to have those reviewed and, when possible, resolved. The procedure indicates that staff should encourage patients to make any issues they have with their care known and outlines how grievances are handled, including final decisions by the Executive Director and access to grievance mechanisms at the state and HRSA levels.

[TEXT] d. Uses Electronic Health Record and Population Management System to Track Risk Factors FPCSN incorporated Centricity into the practice as an EHR and practice management system in 2005. The organization has regularly transitioned to more recent versions of the Centricity Practice Solutions system, converting the EHR to the certified meaningful use version. FPCSN system is now known as AthenaPractice. It is an integrated EHR and practice management system that fully supports the CQI process and is used to track clinical and financial data, providing information on both the clinical outcome measures for all life cycles and the financial goals of the program. The EHR has evidence-based practice standards embedded in the clinical decision support tool, so that those standards, as well as others that the provider staff chooses, can be used for CQI. The Dental Department uses VisDental, a Visualutions product that embeds into AthenaPractice so FPCSN has one EHR for patients using most of its services. Efforts are currently underway to bring behavioral health services into the EHR. This will allow seamless, integrated care for all patients accessing services along with one system for all reporting.

[TEXT] The FPCSN AthenaPractice system contains a complete login and securitylaccess system to meet all HIPAA requirements; integrated MQIC reporting functionality and analysis for Meaningful Use patient care analysis; and reporting, patient registration, scheduling, billing and medical chart tracking in all ambulatory and primary care and behavioral health areas. It is backed by integrated quality reporting metrics, and serves as a self-contained, HIPAA-compliant and Meaningful Use certified product.

[HEADING] 2. Improvement of Clinical Quality and Health Outcomes

[TEXT] FPCSN is focused on the quality of the services provided to its patient population and on improving the health of the population of the area served. Standards for treatment for a number of chronic conditions are embedded in the EHR and preventive and treatment services and outcomes are reviewed through peer reviews and individual provider dashboards.

[HEADING] a. Body Mass Index (BMI) Screening and Follow-Up Plan

[TEXT] The population being served by FPCSN has a number of health-related social needs that are barriers to the maintenance of a healthy weight. The population largely lives in poverty, has a high prevalence of obesity, and lacks knowledge about and access to healthy food and many live in areas where it is unsafe to spend time outdoors exercising. FPCSN has an Overweight and Obesity in Adults Clinical Practice Protocol to give provider and patient teams need guidance and support to assure that medical care and follow up consistently follow evidence-based guidelines. The Protocol includes the requirement that all patients with BMI > 30 with or without co-morbidities are defined as high risk and referred to the RN Care Manager, the Behavioral Health Consultant, and the Nutritionist/Diabetic Educator who provides the nutrition/physical activity counseling. Patients with a BMI > 25 with co-morbidities are defined as moderate risk and referred to the above support staff as needed plus provided the nutrition/physical activity counseling. All BMIs > 25 and BMIs < 18.5 or 22 (per age group) are incorporated into the obesity-overweight/underweight dashboard and individual provider reports are provided to the providers on a quarterly basis to allow recall for any risk category as needed.

========== PAGE 48 (from PDF footer) ==========

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242645

[TEXT] Grant Number: N/A

[HEADING] Family Practice & Counseling Services Network 2026 Service Area Competition Application

[TEXT] Many patients have difficulty following through with their care plans and need additional counseling and support to follow the regime to manage their weight. The Nutritionist and/or diabetic educator make outreach/recall efforts with patients with moderate or high risk who have not been seen in at least a quarter. They are encouraged to come in for care and ongoing counseling regarding their care plans. Healthy eating is a priority for FPCSN. One site initiated a Food Access in the Community Team (FACT) group and partnered with Philabundance to become a food distribution site and now food pantries and WIC are on-site at each of the three comprehensive sites to help address food insecurity.

[HEADING] b. Breast, Cervical, and Colorectal Cancer Screenings

[TEXT] FPCSN was awarded Accelerating Cancer Screening (AxCS) funding in 2024 to increase colorectal cancer screening and referral in collaboration with the Spectrum FQHC, the Philadelphia Health Federation and its HCCN, and the Penn Abramson Cancer Center. The partnering organizations are focusing on unscreened patients of the participating centers, including over five thousand Philadelphia residents, who experience multiple barriers to health care services. Through centralized use of population health management systems, the project team developed outreach lists for mailings that include patient education and a FIT kit, thus enabling a broad, efficient approach to addressing gaps in preventive screening. Text messages informed by behavioral science encourage patients to use the FIT kits and mail back their tests. The health centers' systems are being used to track and follow-up on results. The Cancer Center supports the health centers with expertise in mailed FIT campaigns as well as through a contracted Navigator who provides intensive, personalized services to patients who have a positive FIT and need colonoscopy and possible follow-up care. Through this methodology, the partnering organizations expect to double rates of colorectal cancer screening. The project is testing the viability of centralized, technology-enabled outreach for cancer screening, in order to support enhanced capacity for navigation services in FQHCs.

[TEXT] FPCSN has a Women's Health Clinical Practice Protocol to give provider and patient teams guidance and support to assure that medical care and follow up consistently follow evidence- based guidelines. The Protocol includes a workflow that dictates all women with appointments for family planning who have not had timely Pap tests or mammograms will have Pap tests set up in the exam room before the provider comes in. Those who need mammograms will receive a referral to their imaging center of choice. FPCSN has a Women's Health team, consisting of a women's health NP and a medical assistant, who recall women who have not come in for Pap tests as needed and rotate among the Philadelphia sites to conduct these. Patients often resist these tests and do not understand the importance of screening. Since the time recommended between tests has increased, some patients forget about them. Patients who are due for testing receive outreach/recall messages to schedule tests. FPCSN is learning from the formal work being done around colorectal screening and will apply that learning to Pap testing as well.

[HEADING] c. Diabetes and Hypertension Control

[TEXT] The population being served by FPCSN has a number of health-related social needs that are barriers to the maintenance of a healthy weight and the management of diabetes and hypertension. The population largely lives in poverty, has a high prevalence of obesity, and lacks knowledge about the dangers of their condition. There is also a lack of knowledge about advances in diabetic treatment such as weekly injections that can help patients more easily manage their disease. It has also been demonstrated that stress can contribute to poor

FPCSN is working to address social needs as part of its approach to controlling these conditions and educating patients on the impact they have on physical health.

[TEXT] FPCSN has a number of resources available to assist individuals in need of help in controlling their weight, their blood pressure, or their HbA1c levels. The FPCSN Clinical Practice Protocols for Diabetes and Hypertension give provider and patient teams guidance and support to assure that medical care and follow up consistently follow evidence-based guidelines. These efforts have been expanded to all three comprehensive sites and to prenatal patients as well.

Healthy eating is a priority for FPCSN. [HEADING] d. Screening for Depression and Follow-Up Planning

[TEXT] FPCSN has had behavioral health counseling in place since the inception of the health center and has been a pioneer in the integration of behavioral health services with primary care. FPCSN has a Depression Screening Clinical Practice Protocol in place to give provider and patient teams guidance and support to assure that care and follow up consistently follow evidence-based guidelines. Behavioral Health Consultant services are embedded in primary care to provide additional assessment, brief intervention, and referral to more intensive services. Psychiatric Nurse Practitioners are also embedded in primary care at our three comprehensive sites for patients who are in need of medication management. Patients can be referred by these BH providers or their primary care provider to FPCSN Outpatient located within the three comprehensive sites and will soon be available in the Mill Creek site as well. Outpatient services are provided by clinical psychologists, licensed professional counselors, psychiatric nurse practitioners, and licensed clinical social workers, as well as psychiatrists.

[TEXT] Screening for depression, other mental health issues, and substance use issues is completed on tablets every six months as part of the FPCSN registration system. This has significantly increased the number of patients screened and identified for intervention. Managers are working to

[HEADING] GOVERNANCE

[HEADING] 1. Governing Board Reflection of the Community and Engagement with Patients

[TEXT] As noted in Form 6A, 50% of the 12 members of the FPCSN Board of Directors are current users of the health center's services. One member is a representative of the Housing Authority and two others are or have been public housing residents. Most of the members live and/or work in the service area and several have expertise in community engagement. The patient Board members report on their experiences as patients, from the time they walk into the health center and encounter the person registering them through checkout, allowing management and fellow members to get accurate feedback on patient appointments. All of the Board members are active members of the community and they seek out people in the area to assure they are aware of the health center and to learn of any concerns there might be about services provided. Those who are not patients share their experiences and the opinions they gather outside of the health center.

[HEADING] a. The Board Leverages Members' Expertise

[TEXT] All but one of the FPCSN board members live and/or work in the area served and they include individuals with expertise in law, public relations, education, community engagement, and healthcare operations and strategy. The Board members are eager to share their expertise and their input is welcomed by management as well as their fellow Board members. The Board's varying expertise will guide FPCSN strategic direction through program design, community

[TEXT] engagement, and public health initiatives. At each Board meeting, there is a discussion of sharing resources among board members that could be utilized at the health centers.

[TEXT] b. The Board Provides Oversight and Strategic Direction

[TEXT] The FPCSN Bylaws indicate the Board is responsible for strategic planning and monitoring of program progress on those plans. The needs assessment of the service area community and the ongoing collaboration with the Housing Authority and other community partners are used by the Board for strategic planning. The information provided to the Board for strategic planning includes information on the health center's performance improvement activities, which include utilization and outcomes data. The members of the Board who are users of FPCSN services and those with connections in the community bring valuable information to this process. The Board utilizes the strategic plan as the blueprint for increasing and improving service to the community. The review of progress toward strategic plan goals, along with the reports from the CQI process, are mechanisms for the Board's use in its ongoing monitoring of organizational services, meeting the needs of the community, and patient satisfaction.

[TEXT] c. The Board Evaluates Financial and Quality Performance

[TEXT] The FPCSN Bylaws indicate the Board is responsible to evaluate the quality of the work of the health center and provide for organizational stability and compliance. The Board approves the fiscal year budget and CQI plan yearly. Quality Improvement reports, including progress on clinical and financial performance measures, incidents, and patient and staff satisfaction, are made to the board quarterly. The Board receives regular updates on the CQI process, which allows them to be aware of patient outcomes and satisfaction and any incidents that pose risk to the organization. The FPCSN management and the Board work closely together to manage the finances of the health center. The fiscal management policies and procedures have been approved by the Board and are reviewed annually. Monthly reports are provided to the CEO and are reviewed during regular management meetings and Board meetings. This financial information is used for decision-making regarding programs, staffing, and monitoring of the Financial Performance measures.

[TEXT] 3. Native American Tribe Applicants - NA

[TEXT] 4. Competing Supplement Applicants - NA

[TEXT] 5. Public Agency Applicants - NA

[HEADING] SUPPORT REQUESTED

[TEXT] Complete budget materials for the year of the project period are included in this application, as are the staffing and income analysis forms. The budget assumptions are reasonable, given the number of users and the number of billable visits, as well as the severity of the health problems experienced by the people being served. The number of patients projected to be served is the same as the number listed as the SAAT patient target. The budgeted expenses, including salaries, benefits, and other supply and administrative costs, are reasonable for the size of the health center and the volume and types of services to be provided. Salaries and fringes represent half of the overall expenses. FPCSN is operated in a way that maximizes non-grant revenue and leverages other resources, particularly patient service fees and 340B funds, for health center operations. The percentage of federal grant dollars in the overall budget has always been reasonable and was 19% of the budget in the most recent year.

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242645 Grant Number: N/A Docusign Envelope ID: DA986F84-D034-4883-85C0-FFDA2F3166FF

[HEADING] Bylaws Family Practice & Counseling Services Network

[HEADING] Article I: Mission and Activities

[TEXT] Mission. Family Practice & Counseling Services Network (FPCSN) provides person-centered, integrated and comprehensive health services to individuals and families across their lifespan. FPCSN promotes an antiracist, trauma-informed culture, as well as resiliency and well-being among patients, staff and surrounding communities.

[TEXT] Activities. The activities of the Corporation shall be those necessary and appropriate to accomplish the purposes of the Corporation as stated in these Bylaws and in the Articles of Incorporation.

[HEADING] Article II: Offices

[TEXT] Offices. The principal office of the Corporation shall be 4700 Wissahickon Avenue, Suite 118, Philadelphia, PA 19144 or such other place as shall be designated by the Board of Directors.

[TEXT] Article III: Board of Directors

[TEXT] Number and Composition

[TEXT] The Board of Directors will consist of at least nine (9) but not more than twenty-five (25) members.

[TEXT] Composition. The Board of Directors shall have the following composition:

[TEXT] a) At least fifty-one percent (51%) of the directors shall be patients served by the Corporation's health center and who, as a group, demographically represent the individuals served by the health center and should include representation from public housing. A patient is an individual who has received at least one service from the health center in the past twenty-four (24) months that generated a health center visit, where both the service and the site where the service was received are with the health center's scope of project as approved by the Health Resources and Services Administration.

[TEXT] b) No more than fifty percent (50%) of the remaining directors may be individuals who derive more than ten percent (10%) of their annual income from the health care industry. The remaining directors shall be representative of the community in which the Corporation's health center is located, including public housing and shall be selected for their expertise in community affairs, local government, finance and banking, legal affairs, and other commercial and industrial concerns, or social service agencies within the community.

[TEXT] c) The Chief Executive Officer may only serve as a non-voting, ex-officio member of the Board.

[TEXT] d) Qualifications: All Board members shall meet the following additional minimal qualifications:

[TEXT] a. Members shall be residents of Philadelphia or state of PA and at least eighteen (21)

[TEXT] Powers of Board of Directors. Subject to the limitation of law, or the Articles of Incorporation and of these Bylaws, all corporate powers shall be exercised by or under authority of, and the business and affairs of the Corporation shall be controlled by a Board of Directors.

[TEXT] Election; Term of Office. The Directors shall be elected by a vote of the majority of the Directors at a Board meeting.

[TEXT] There is no term of office for FPCSN Board of Directors.

[TEXT] Vacancies. Any vacancy occurring in the Board of Directors may be filled by the Board of Directors or, if the directors remaining in office constitute less than a quorum, by the affirmative vote of a majority of the remaining directors. Candidates shall be nominated by the directors remaining in office. No reduction of the number of directors shall have the effect of removing any director prior to the expiration of their term of office.

[TEXT] Removal of Directors. Any individual director may be removed from office, with or without cause, by a vote of two-thirds (2/3) of the directors then in office. If a director misses three

[TEXT] Regular Meetings. Meetings of the Board of Directors shall be held at least once a month or at such other intervals as determined by the Board of Directors.

[TEXT] Special Meetings. Special meetings of the Board of Directors for any purpose shall be called at any time by the Chairperson or by at least twenty percent (20%) of the directors then in office.

[TEXT] Place of Meetings. Meetings of the Board of Directors shall be held at the principal office of the Corporation or virtually.

[TEXT] Notice of Meetings. Meetings of the Board of Directors may be held without notice, unless as otherwise provided herein.

[TEXT] Any Board of Directors action to remove a director or to approve matters concerning:

[TEXT] a) director's conflict of interest.

[TEXT] b) indemnification.

[TEXT] c) amendment of the Corporation's Articles of Incorporation.

[TEXT] d) a plan of merger or conversion.

[TEXT] e) the sale or mortgage of all or substantially all of the Corporation's assets; or

[TEXT] f) dissolution: shall not be valid unless each director is given at least seven (7) days written notice that the matter will be voted upon at a Board of Directors meeting, unless notice is waived in writing, signed by the director so waiving notice, and filed with the Corporation's minutes.

[TEXT] Action Without a Meeting. Any action required or permitted to be taken by the Board of Directors at a meeting may be taken without a meeting if all directors (i) execute a consent in writing, setting forth the action to be taken, or (ii) transmit an electronic transmission consenting to the action to be taken. The consent shall be included in the minutes or filed with the corporate records reflecting the action taken. Action taken under this Section is effective when the last director signs the consent or gives consent by electronic transmission unless the consent specifies a different effective date.

[TEXT] Participation in Meetings through Electronic Communications. Members of the Board of Directors of the Corporation, or any committee designed by such Board of Directors may participate in a meeting of such Board of Directors or committee through the use of any means of communication including in person or virtual whereby all persons participating in the meeting can simultaneously hear each other, and participation in a meeting in such manner shall constitute presence in person at such meeting.

[TEXT] Quorum and Vote. Fifty-one percent of the current members of the Board of Directors in office immediately before a meeting begins shall constitute a quorum for the transaction of business. When a quorum is present, the affirmative votes of a majority of the directors present at any meeting are required to approve a corporate act. In the absence of a quorum,

[TEXT] Standing Committees. The Board of Directors shall have the following standing committees:

[TEXT] a) Executive Committee. The Executive Committee shall be comprised of the officers of the Corporation elected pursuant to Article V. Subject to any limitations imposed by the Board of Directors, the Executive Committee shall have the power to act on behalf of the entire Board regarding issues which arise during the period between meetings of the Board of Directors. Seventy-five percent of the members of the Executive Committee shall constitute a quorum necessary for transaction of business. If a quorum is present, the affirmative votes of a majority of the members voting on any matter are required to approve any action taken by the Executive Committee on behalf of the Board of Directors.

[TEXT] b) Finance/Audit Committee. The Finance/Audit Committee shall be comprised of the Treasurer and at least one other director. The Finance/Audit Committee shall oversee the fiscal and accounting matters of the Corporation and the audit of the Corporation. The Finance/Audit Committee shall also perform such other appropriate duties as may be prescribed by the Board.

[TEXT] c) Quality Assurance Committee. The Quality Assurance Committee shall be comprised of at least two directors. The Quality Assurance Committee shall monitor and evaluate patient care and identify, study and recommend improvements in the Corporation's patient care delivery process. The Quality Assurance Committee shall also perform such other appropriate duties as may be prescribed by the Board.

[TEXT] Code of Ethics/Conflict of Interest. A strict code of ethics shall exist with the Board of



========== PAGE 70 (from PDF footer) ==========

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242645 Grant Number: N/A Docusign Envelope ID: DA986F84-D034-4883-85C0-FFDA2F3166FF

[TEXT] Directors. Directors are expected to abide by the same Code of Conduct that applies to members of Family Practices and Counseling Network Services Health Center's workforce and disclose any potential conflict of interest prior to participating in the Board of Director's deliberations on any matter in which they may have a personal financial interest. No one may become a director solely for the purpose of furthering his or her individual business or organizational interest. In order to avoid any appearance of any conflict of interest, no director will be permitted to vote or influence the remainder of the directorship vote in his or her behalf on any matter, which would serve his or her individual interest.

[TEXT] Disclosure. The real and potential interests of any director in any financial transaction, contract or agreement arising in the course of affairs of the Corporation shall be fully disclosed to the Board of Directors at the earliest opportunity or practicable date, as set forth in the conflict-of-interest policy adopted by the Board of Directors.

[TEXT] Article V. Officers Designation. The officers of the Corporation shall be a Chairperson, a Secretary and a Treasurer and such other officers as may be designated by the Board of Directors.

[TEXT] Election and Term of Office. Officers shall be elected by members of the Board of Directors at the Annual Meeting or at a special meeting called for that purpose and installed as the first order of business to assume office for the remainder of the meeting. Term of office shall begin with the meeting at which such election occurs and shall be for three (3) years. An officer who has completed two (2) consecutive terms in the same office shall not be re-elected to that office of the ensuing year. No third party may appoint a majority of the total number of health center Board members or a majority of the non-patient members.

[TEXT] Removal and Resignation. Any officer may be removed, with or without cause, by the Board of Directors at any regular or special meeting. Any officer may resign at any time by giving written notice to the Board of Directors or to the Chairperson or to the Secretary of the Corporation. Any such resignation shall take effect at the date of the receipt of such notice or at any later time specified therein, and, unless otherwise specified therein, the acceptance of such resignation shall not be necessary to make it effective. No third party may require the removal of any current Board member not appointment by that party.

[TEXT] Vacancies. Any vacancy in any office because of death, resignation, removal, disqualification or other cause shall be filled in the manner prescribed in these By-Laws for regular appointments to such office.

[TEXT] The Chairperson. The Chairperson shall be selected from the Board of Directors and shall preside over all meetings of the Board of Directors. They shall be kept advised of the general affairs of the Corporation and ensure that all orders, resolutions and policies of the Board of Directors are carried out into effect. They shall chair the Executive Committee and serve as ex-officio member of all other committees. They shall have the usual power and duties customarily vested in the office of the Chairperson. If for any reason it becomes necessary to replace the Chairperson prior to expiration of their term, the Treasurer shall fill the unexpired term, and the Board of Directors shall elect a new Treasurer.

[TEXT] Secretary. The Secretary shall keep, or cause to be kept, a book of minutes, at the principal office or such other place as the Board of Directors may order, of all meetings of directors, with the time and place of holding, whether regular or special, and if special, how authorized the notice thereof given, the names of those present at directors meeting and the proceeding thereof. The Secretary shall keep, or cause to be kept, at the principal office of the Corporation a copy of the Articles of incorporation and By-Laws. The Secretary shall keep a record of the Corporation's directors, showing each director's name and address. The Secretary shall give, or cause to be given, notice of all meetings of the Board of Directors required by the By-Laws or by law to be given and shall have such other powers and perform such other duties as may be prescribed by the Board of Directors or these By-Laws.

[TEXT] Treasurer. The Treasurer shall be the financial and accounting officer of the Corporation. The Treasurer shall monitor the receipt and payment of all the funds of the Corporation in the manner authorized by the Board of Directors. The Treasurer shall cause to be kept a book or books setting forth a true record of receipts and expenditures, assets and liabilities, losses and gains of the Corporation and shall send or cause to be given to the directors such financial statements and reports as required to be given by law, these By-Laws or by the Board of Directors.

[HEADING] Article VI. Corporate Records and Reports

[TEXT] Records. The Corporation shall maintain adequate and correct accounts, books and records of its business and properties and minutes of the proceedings of its Board of Directors. All of such books, records and accounts shall be kept at its principal place of business in the State of Pennsylvania as fixed by the Board of Directors from time to time.

[TEXT] Signing of Checks. All checks, drafts or other orders for payment of money, notes, or other indebtedness, issued in the name of or payable to the Corporation shall be signed or endorsed by such person or persons and in such manner as shall be determined from time to time by resolution of the Board of Directors.

[TEXT] Execution of Contracts. The Board of Directors may authorize any one or more officers, employees or agents to enter any contract or execute any instrument on behalf of the Corporation. Unless so authorized, no officer, agent or employee shall have any power or authority to bind the Corporation by any contract or engagement or to pledge its credit or to render it liable for any purpose or to any amount.

[TEXT] Annual Reports. The Board of Directors shall cause an annual report to be delivered to the Director of the Department of Commerce and Consumer Affairs for filing as required by law.

[TEXT] Article VII. Indemnification of Directors and Officers

[TEXT] Indemnification. To the fullest extent permitted by Pennsylvania law, the Corporation shall indemnify each director, officer and employee of the Corporation who is or was a party or is threatened to be made a party to any threatened, pending or completed action, suit or proceeding, whether civil, criminal, administrative or investigative and whether formal or informal, because such person is or was a director, officer or employee of the Corporation, or

[TEXT] Advances for Expenses. The Corporation shall advance funds to pay for or reimburse the reasonable expenses and attorneys' fees incurred by a director, officer or employee before final disposition of an action, suit or proceeding, provided that such person delivers a written affirmation of such person's good faith belief that such person has met the requisite standard of conduct for indemnification and delivers a written undertaking to repay such amount if it is ultimately determined that such person did not meet the standard of conduct.

[TEXT] Continuing Indemnification. The indemnification shall be cumulative and not exclusive, and shall be in addition to any other indemnification provided by law or by any other agreement. Any repeal, amendment or modification of this Article shall not affect the indemnification provided in this Article for any acts or omissions occurring prior to such repeal, amendment or modification. The indemnification provided for in this Article shall continue as to any person who has ceased to be a director, officer or employee of the Corporation and shall inure to the benefit of such person's heirs, personal representatives, executors and administrators.

[TEXT] Insurance. The Corporation shall have the power to purchase and maintain insurance on behalf of any person who is or was a director, officer or employee of the Corporation, or is or was serving at the request of the Corporation as a director, officer or employee of another corporation, partnership, joint venture, trust or other enterprise against any liability asserted against him and incurred by him in any such capacity or arising out of his status as such, whether or not the Corporation would have the power to indemnify him against such liability under the provisions of this Article VII.

[HEADING] Article VIII. Amendment to By-Laws

[TEXT] Amendment by Majority Vote. The By-Laws of this Corporation may from time to time be repealed, amended or altered, or new By-Laws may be adopted by the Board of Directors.

[TEXT] Limitation on Amendment. Anything herein to the contrary notwithstanding, these By- Laws shall not be amended in any manner which: alters the basic purpose of the Corporation as set forth herein and in the Articles of Incorporation, conflicts with any applicable law or government regulation; causes the diversion of any part of the Corporation for the purposes other than those authorized herein, deprives any eligible beneficiary of benefits; or causes the Corporation to lose its tax exempt status under State and Federal laws.

[HEADING] Article IX. Dispute Resolution

[TEXT] Any and all disputes between or among any parties to these By-Laws or anyone claiming rights by, through or under any parties to these By-Laws that arise from or in any way relate to these By-Laws or any of their subject matter will be resolved by mediation pursuant to

The arbitration award will be final and binding and will be enforceable as and by a court with jurisdiction over the parties.

[HEADING] Article X. Legal Standing

[TEXT] If any part of these By-Laws is illegal or invalid, such illegality or invalidity shall not affect the remaining parts of these By-Laws, unless such illegality or invalidity prevents the Board of Directors from accomplishing the purposes of the Corporation. If any illegality or invalidity exists, the Board of Directors shall immediately make the necessary amendments to eliminate the illegality or invalidity, and shall promulgate a new legal provision as similar as possible to the illegal or invalid provision, keeping the intent, as close as possible, of the illegal or invalid provision.

[HEADING] Preservation of Confidential Information.
