[HEADING] CHIEF EXECUTIVE OFFICER

[TEXT] The Chief Executive Officer (CEO) upholds the mission, values and principles of the organization and provides evidenced- based strategic vision, leadership, direction and oversight of all aspects of Family Practice & Counseling Services Network (FPCSN). This includes organizational operations to manage financial health, employee well-being, quality services, compliance, brand identity, compliance, and overall organizational strategy. The CEO serves as the face of the organization with internal and external stakeholders and provides communication between board members and FPCSN executives. The CEO is directly employed by the health center and reports directly to the governing Board of Directors. ESSENTIAL DUTIES and RESPONSIBILITIES STRATEGIC LEADERSHIP

[TEXT]  Builds, leads, and manages the Executive Team, delegating authority and ensuring effective collaboration to cultivate and maintain high performing Executive and Leadership Teams.

[TEXT]  In collaboration with the Executive Team, provides visionary, strategic and innovative leadership ensuring alignment with FPCSN vision, mission, and long-term goals, and strategies.

[TEXT]  Leads, fosters and ensures accountability for a value-driven, equitable work environment for staff and patients. OPERATIONAL OVERSIGHT

[TEXT]  Collaborates with the Chief Operations Officer to ensure operational efficiency and effectiveness, ensuring alignment with the overall strategy of FPCSN.

[TEXT]  Collaborates with the Chief Clinical Officer to ensure high quality of care, fiscally responsible services and a high degree of patient satisfaction.

[TEXT]  Collaborates with the Executives, Senior Leaders and Board of Directors to set the course for health center expansion to new sites and new services/programs in response to community needs.

[TEXT] FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT

[TEXT] . Collaborates with the Chief Financial Officer to ensure sound fiscal operations and long-term sustainability.

[TEXT]  Oversight for the budget, financial planning, and resource allocation of FPCSN to ensure profitability and growth, grants and reporting are completed accurately and in a timely manner.

[TEXT] BOARD GOVERNANCE & STAKEHOLDER RELATIONS

[TEXT]  Engages with and informs the Board on Directors of FPCSNs operations and performance.

[TEXT]  Maintains relationships with the board of directors, funders, key partners, and other stakeholders.

[TEXT]  Fosters and maintains community partnerships and collaborations to provide services responsive to the community and staff.

[TEXT] PUBLIC REPRESENTATION

[TEXT]  Acts as the primary public face of FPCSN for media, public events, and other community relations.

[TEXT]  Represents FPCSN at the local, state and national levels and serves as the primary spokesperson for FPCSN.

[TEXT]  Participates in advocacy efforts for community health centers

[TEXT] POLICY AND COMPLIANCE

[TEXT] . Collaborates with the Chief Compliance Officer, ensures and maintains compliance with all federal, state and local regulatory standards.

[TEXT] . Collaborates with the Chief Human Resources Officer to ensure adherence to FPCSNs policies and procedures and a high degree of employee engagement.

[HEADING] QUALITY & HEALTH INFORMATION

[TEXT]  Collaborates with the Chief Information Officer to ensure a robust, technically-sound, compliant information system and strategy in support of the business initiatives relative to security and maintenance of the technology network.  Serves on the CQI Committee, assuring that there is an annual plan approved by the Board of Directors.

[TEXT] QUALIFICATIONS

[TEXT]  Minimum of a Master's Degree in Public Health or Management field

[TEXT]  Minimum of three to five years in senior management in a non-profit, community organization

[TEXT]  Exhibit behaviors that align with FPCSN's organizational values, mission, and beliefs

[TEXT]  Demonstrate cultural competence/proficiency in interactions with others by treating co-workers, colleagues and those receiving service with respect and fairness at all times

[TEXT]  Ability to build and maintain positive and professional relationships based on respect, trust, and safety

[TEXT]  Demonstrate exemplary problem-solving, communication, interpersonal, and conflict resolution skills.

[TEXT]  Ability to work effectively as a team member

[TEXT]  High level of integrity. Highly responsible and reliable

[TEXT]  Exemplary organizational skills and ability to prioritize

[TEXT]  Commitment to service excellence for underrepresented and underserved populations

[HEADING] CHIEF CLINICAL OFFICER

[TEXT] The Chief Clinical Officer upholds the mission and values of FPCSN by overseeing all Clinical Departments and assuring the delivery of all clinical care is high quality, evidence-based, satisfying to patients and staff, and cost-effective; promotes a fiscally sound organization. [TEXT] Description: University of Pennsylvania Health System (UPHS) accepts referrals of patients for emergency, outpatient, and inpatient medical services regardless of ability to pay. The agreement details the services provided, including prenatal, intrapartum, and postnatal care, as well as provision of information between FPCSN and UPHS and referral of patients back to FPCSN. [HEADING] CITY OF PHILADELPHIA

[TEXT] DEPARTMENT OF PUBLIC HEALTH AMBULATORY HEALTH SERVICES 1101 Market Street, 11th Floor Philadelphia, Pennsylvania 19107 Tel: (215) 685-6769 Fax (215) 685-6732

[TEXT] Palak Raval-Nelson, PhD, MPH Health Commissioner

[TEXT] Cheryl Kramer-Sylvester, MBA Director - Ambulatory Health Services

[TEXT] September 16, 2025

[TEXT] Emily Nichols, MPH Chief Executive Officer Family Practice & Counseling Services Network, Inc. 4700 Wissahickon Avenue, Suite 118 Philadelphia, PA 19144

[TEXT] Dear Ms. Nichols,

[TEXT] On behalf of Philadelphia Department of Public Health (PDPH), I write in full support of the Service Area Competition application submitted by the Family Practice & Counseling Services Network (FPCSN) to the Health Resources and Services Administration (HRSA). For more than 33 years, FPCSN has been a vital presence in Philadelphia's healthcare landscape, first as a Federally Qualified Health Center as part of Resources for Human Development, and now as a standalone non-profit Community Health Center. Throughout this legacy of providing care, FPCSN has consistently upheld the standards and requirements of the HRSA Health Center Program, providing essential care to communities across Philadelphia.

[TEXT] Recent analyses confirm the significant unmet need for primary care in West/Southwest and North Philadelphia, where the FPCSN service area is located. In 2023, the Federally Qualified Health Centers served just 38.7% of the population in these neighborhoods, leaving an estimated 298,000 individuals without access to care through a community health center. These communities face well-documented challenges, including higher rates of chronic illness, limited preventive and oral healthcare, and gaps in prenatal and behavioral health services.

[TEXT] PDPH operates nine FQHC/Look Alike heath centers that serve the entire City, and our experience affirms the magnitude of the need. The demand for high-quality, affordable, and accessible primary care far exceeds the current capacity. FPCSN's comprehensive model, which integrates primary care, behavioral health, oral health, and wellness services, strengthens the overall safety net and improves access for patients who might otherwise go without needed care.

[TEXT] PDPH and FPCSN have long collaborated through the Health Federation of Philadelphia and the Pennsylvania Association of Community Health Centers (PACHC). We share a mission to expand healthcare access, ensuring that care is delivered with dignity and respect. PDPH is committed to continuing this partnership, recognizing that collective effort is essential to meeting the health needs of our region.

[TEXT] For these reasons, I strongly support FPCSN's Service Area Competition application. I am confident that, with HRSA's continued support, FPCSN will sustain and expand its impact as an essential healthcare provider for Philadelphia and its surrounding communities.

[TEXT] Sincerely,

[TEXT] Cheryl Kramer-Sylvester Director, Ambulatory Health Services Cheryl Kramer-Sylvester

[TEXT] The Health Federation is a HRSA-funded HCCN, as well as a membership network of the FQHCs in Southeastern Pennsylvania. HFP has a long history of working collaboratively with FPCSN and its other members in many areas, including health information technology, quality improvement, and projects to improve chronic and infectious disease management.

[TEXT] For these reasons, I strongly support FPCSN's Service Area Competition application. I am confident that, with HRSA's continued support, FPCSN will sustain and expand its impact as an essential healthcare provider for Philadelphia and its surrounding communities.

[TEXT] Sincerely,

[TEXT] On behalf of Penn Medicine, I am writing to express my strong support for the Family Practice & Counseling Services Network (FPCSN) in their application to the Health Resources and Services Administration's (HRSA) Service Area Competition (SAC) (HRSA 26-004). Throughout this legacy, FPCSN has consistently exceeded standards and requirements of the HRSA Health Center Program, delivering high-quality, comprehensive care to communities across Philadelphia and Delaware County.

[TEXT] Penn Medicine shares FPCSN's unwavering commitment to advancing access to high-quality health care for all. FPCSN has demonstrated a long and successful history of providing patient centered, affordable care to medical underserved populations. Their integrated model, which combines primary care, behavioral health, and supportive services, reflects best practices for improving health outcomes, addressing the social determinants of health, and reducing health disparities.

[TEXT] Our organizations have collaborated closely to coordinate care for patients with complex medical and social needs, reduce avoidable emergency department utilization, and strengthen linkages between hospital-based and community-based care. Through shared clinical programming, such as community-based prenatal care and integrated behavioral healthcare, we have seen firsthand the impact of FPCSN's patient-centered model of care.

[TEXT] FPCSN represents the best of what community health centers offer - trusted, efficient, and compassionate care that empowers patients and strengthens neighborhoods. HRSA support will enable FPCSN to expand and sustain their essential services, build organizational capacity, and ensure that even more individuals and families can access comprehensive and affordable care, close to home.

[TEXT] Thank you for your consideration and for your ongoing commitment to supporting organizations that serve the most vulnerable members of our communities

[TEXT] Dear Ms. Nichols,

[TEXT] On behalf of the Philadelphia Housing Authority (PHA), I write in full support of the Service Area Competition application submitted by the Family Practice & Counseling Services Network (FPCSN) to the Health Resources and Services Administration (HRSA). For more than 33 years, FPCSN has been a vital presence in Philadelphia's healthcare landscape, first as a Federally Qualified Health Center as part of Resources for Human Development, and now as a standalone non-profit Community Health Center. Throughout this legacy of providing care, FPCSN has consistently upheld the standards and requirements of the HRSA Health Center Program, providing essential care to communities across Philadelphia. The FPCSN service sites are accessible to many of the PHA public housing and the service area includes West/Southwest Philadelphia, an area the City has found to be without adequate access to primary health care.

[TEXT] PHA is concerned about the health problems experienced by the public housing and low-income communities that FPCSN serves. FPCSN services have long been targeted to residents of public housing and the surrounding communities, which face well-documented challenges, including higher rates of chronic illness, limited preventive and oral healthcare, and gaps in prenatal and behavioral health services. The area FQHCs serve just 38.7% of the population in these neighborhoods, leaving an estimated 298,000 individuals without access to care through a community health center.

[TEXT] The demand for high-quality, affordable, and accessible primary care far exceeds the current capacity in Philadelphia. FPCSN's comprehensive model, which integrates primary care, behavioral health, oral health, and wellness services, strengthens the overall safety net and improves access for patients who might otherwise go without needed care. PHA depends upon FPCSN's expertise and has a long collaborative relationship with your health centers. FPCSN sites are noted on the PHA website among the trusted resources there.

[TEXT] For these reasons, I strongly support FPCSN's Service Area Competition application. I am confident that, with HRSA's continued support, FPCSN will sustain and expand its impact as an essential healthcare provider for Philadelphia and its surrounding communities.

[TEXT] Sincerely,

[TEXT] Kelvin A. Jeremiah, President & CEO Philadelphia Housing Authority

[TEXT] The Pennsylvania Department of Human Services (PA DHS) is submitting this letter of support regarding Family Practice & Counseling Services Network, Inc. Service Are Competition Application to the Health Resources and Services Administration (HRSA). PA DHS supports the supply and distribution of primary care practitioners, particularly in underserved areas, that align with the Pennsylvania Medical Assistance (MA, also known as Medicaid), the HealthChoices mandatory MA managed care program and the Children's Health Insurance Program (CHIP). FPCSN has a history of supporting the Philadelphia area as a Federally Qualified Health Care Center (FQHC) and seeks to achieve that status again.

[TEXT] The PA DHS Office of Medical Assistance Programs continually assesses and seeks to assure both a sufficient supply of primary care practitioners and an appropriate level of access to primary care for all MA and CHIP beneficiaries and works to accomplish those aims through a number of program areas. One of the important elements in the overall approach to providing health care to underserved populations is the role of the community health centers. These centers are specifically tasked to provide health care to individuals who receive their coverage through MA. PA DHS supports the mission and goals of the community health centers and their goals of providing health care services, primary care, behavioral health care and oral health to those who need it in their communities.

[TEXT] We look forward to collaborating and continuing to work with FPCSN as a community health center and again as a FQHC in the Philadelphia area to improve the health of Pennsylvania's MA and CHIP beneficiaries.

[TEXT] I write in support of Family Practice & Counseling Services Network's (FPCSN) application for the Service Area Competition grant. This funding would support FPCN's dedication to providing care in their community through primary, behavioral, and oral health services.

[TEXT] FPCSN is a network of federally qualified community health centers that use a nurse-managed, integrated model to deliver coordinated care for the entirety of the patient. For more than three decades, FPCSN has stood as a trusted partner in advancing community health across Philadelphia and continues to advocate for access to affordable, high-quality care.

[TEXT] There is a well-documented need for this type of comprehensive, coordinated care that FPCSN provides; the communities they serve face disproportionately high rates of chronic disease, significant gaps in prenatal and preventive services, and ongoing barriers to accessing essential healthcare.

[TEXT] With this grant funding, FPCSN can also strengthen outreach and care coordination, ensuring that uninsured and underinsured patients remain connected to continuous, comprehensive services rather than falling through the cracks of the healthcare system. Additionally, the funding would enable FPCSN to provide comprehensive care to uninsured patients who would otherwise go without critical primary, behavioral, and oral health services.

[TEXT] Dear Applicant:

[TEXT] We're pleased to tell you we determined you're exempt from federal income tax under Internal Revenue Code (IRC) Section 501(c)(3). Donors can deduct contributions they make to you under IRC Section 170. You're also qualified to receive tax deductible bequests, devises, transfers or gifts under Section 2055, 2106, or 2522. This letter could help resolve questions on your exempt status. Please keep it for your records.

[TEXT] Organizations exempt under IRC Section 501(c)(3) are further classified as either public charities or private foundations. We determined you're a public charity under the IRC Section listed at the top of this letter.

[TEXT] If we indicated at the top of this letter that you're required to file Form 990/990-EZ/990-N, our records show you're required to file an annual information return (Form 990 or Form 990-EZ) or electronic notice (Form 990-N, the e-Postcard). If you don't file a required return or notice for three consecutive years, your exempt status will be automatically revoked.

[TEXT] If we indicated at the top of this letter that an addendum applies, the enclosed addendum is an integral part of this letter.

[TEXT] For important information about your responsibilities as a tax-exempt organization, go to www.irs.gov/charities. Enter "4221-PC" in the search bar to view Publication 4221-PC, Compliance Guide for 501(c)(3) Public Charities, which describes your recordkeeping, reporting, and disclosure requirements.

[TEXT] Sincerely, stephen a. martin

[HEADING] Family Practice & Counseling Services Network 2026 Service Area Competition Application

[HEADING] ATTACHMENT 13 - Health Center Program Compliance

[HEADING] SLIDING FEE DISCOUNT PROGRAM

[TEXT] Sliding Fee Applicability, Definitions, and Alignment with FPG

[TEXT] FPCSN policy, approved by the Board, is that all required primary, preventive, dental, behavioral health, and additional health services are available and accessible to the target population without regard to patients' ability to pay, and that the health center has a sliding fee discount scale geared to U.S. poverty guidelines. It is the policy of FPCSN to uniformly apply fee discounts to all patients deemed eligible, based on the most recent Federal Poverty Guidelines.

[TEXT] The FPCSN sliding scale is based solely on income and family size and is reviewed periodically regarding affordability. The definitions used in the policy for income and family are those of the US Census. Income is defined as all cash receipts before taxes with certain adjustments and does not include non-cash benefits such as SNAP, school lunch programs, clothing vouchers, or food/rent in lieu of wages. Family is defined as a group of two or more persons related by birth, marriage, or adoption who live together; students, regardless of residence, who are supported by their parents are considered to be living in same household. An individual living alone or in a household with individuals outside of their family is defined as a family of one.

[TEXT] Sliding Fee Assessment

[TEXT] FPCSN policy requires that patients are made aware of the sliding fee discount program by providing information on the health center website, posting signs in each site, and notifying patients during appointment scheduling and registration. Patients are asked annually to provide their family size and income information for an assessment of their eligibility for discounted fees. Patients applying for the sliding fee scale discount must present income documentation to determine income level that includes: previous year's tax return, current pay stub, pension check stub, beneficiary award letter (Social Security benefits, etc.), or personal attestation of earnings for persons with no tax liability and/or who are self-employed. If patients do not have proper documentation with them, they are provided time to provide it for the discount to be applied to the visit. Once a discount has been approved, it is honored for a year, at which time the patient must reapply. Patients have the right to refuse to complete the assessment; they will be ineligible for discounts.

[TEXT] Sliding Fee Schedule Structure and Nominal Fees

[TEXT] FPCN has sliding fee scales for Primary Care, Behavioral Health, Integrated Behavioral Health, and Dental services. The FPCSN sliding scales are revised annually and approved by the Board, and include three categories between 100% and 200% of federal poverty level, includes definitions of family size, and is used for all clinical services. (See sliding scale in Attachment 10) The scales and procedures are on hand for staff who register patients and they receive training in how charges are adjusted according to health center policy. The scales are embedded within the EHR to automatically calculate the discounts once family size and income are entered.

[TEXT] Charges for patients with income below 100% of poverty are set at nominal levels that can be waived in some cases. The nominal charges are flat charges, are not set at the actual cost of the service provided, and are set at levels designed to be nominal from the perspective of the patient.

[TEXT] 1



========== PAGE 131 (from PDF footer) ==========

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242645

[TEXT] Grant Number: N/A

[HEADING] Family Practice & Counseling Services Network 2026 Service Area Competition Application

[TEXT] The sliding scales go up to 200% of federal poverty level for most services and 250% for family planning services covered by a state program, and the scales are used for all clinical services. There is no charge for lab work for uninsured patients and it is included as a part of the primary care visit. Attempts are made to collect the discounted fees, but patients are not refused care as a result of non-payment. Hence, no one is denied services due to their inability to pay.

[HEADING] KEY MANAGEMENT STAFF

[TEXT] As noted in Form 2, the organization chart, the position descriptions, and the key management resumes attached, all of the managers, including the Executive Director who is the CEO, are hired directly by FPCSN. The Executive Director reports directly to the Board and the Board has the authority and responsibility for the selection/dismissal and evaluation of that position. The Executive Director is responsible to select and dismiss all personnel working in the health center and to assure there is a process for filling vacant key management positions. The Executive Director supervises the other members of the executive team and assures that Board policies are carried out.

[HEADING] CONTRACTS AND SUBAWARDS

[TEXT] As noted in the narrative, Attachment 7, and Form 8, Family Practice & Counseling Services Network is a private 501(c)3 organization registered in Pennsylvania and with the IRS. FPCSN does not have a parent, affiliate, or subsidiary organization. It has no contracts with any other organization to perform substantive programmatic work within the proposed scope of project, and no subawards to carry out any portion of the project.

[TEXT] FPCSN financial accounting and internal control systems are designed to ensure that all federal funds are fully accounted for, including maintaining source documentation, that all expenditures of federal award funds are allowable, and that only actual work performed is charged to any award. Federal funds received will be tracked in a separate general ledger account. Salaries and wages supported by federal funds will be recorded in these separate general ledger accounts, while other non-personnel costs are reported in a separate cost center.

[HEADING] COLLABORATIVE RELATIONSHIPS

[TEXT] As noted in the narrative and Attachment 9, FPCSN coordinates and integrates its activities with other health services in the service area, consistent with those noted in Attachment 1. The health care community in the Philadelphia area solidly supports the new entity operating the health center.

[HEADING] BILLING AND COLLECTIONS

[TEXT] a. Participation in Medicare, Medicaid, Children's Health Insurance Program (CHIP) As noted in Form 3, FPCSN participates in Medicare, Medicaid, and CHIP, and other insurers. It has contracts with all MCOs in the service area. FPCSN's eligibility determination process allows patients to have their insurance eligibility assessed prior to receiving services. The eligibility verification is completed via an Internet capability utilizing a combination of AthenaPractice eligibility, Promise (State Medicaid) Eligibility, and Navinet eligibility verification portals. The billing process involves claims being submitted to the payors utilizing the ANSI 837 standard format. The claims, automatically generated by the system, are reviewed manually by personnel for accuracy and consistency of coding. All billing is done in-house. Claims are submitted from the practice management system(s) to the payor, utilizing a

[TEXT] 2



========== PAGE 132 (from PDF footer) ==========

[TEXT] EHB Application Number: 242645

[TEXT] Grant Number: N/A

[HEADING] Family Practice & Counseling Services Network 2026 Service Area Competition Application

[TEXT] clearinghouse, which in turn forwards the ANSI 837 file to the payor. The submission of the file is monitored from FPCSN's system to the clearinghouse and from the clearinghouse to the payor, as is the file for a claims acknowledgement from the payor. FPCSN has implemented a full EDI process for claims and reimbursement (including claims payment posting for about 75% of all payments) and is in the process of having all reimbursements where applicable done through electronic funds transfer.

[HEADING] b. Patient Payment Collection and Waiver

[TEXT] The FPCSN policy includes an Eligibility Determination process under which all patients have their eligibility for coverage checked prior to services being performed. Staff update each patient's insurance coverage at the time of the initial call for an appointment and also at the time of the reminder call. Upon the patient's arrival, the staff completes an eligibility verification. Some of the database systems in place are with the Pennsylvania Department of Human Services, the Medicaid MCO, Navinet, and various other Internet capabilities.

[TEXT] FPCSN collections procedures require that patients are asked for applicable co-pays and sliding fee amounts at the time of services. Patients who indicate that they cannot pay the amount owed may have a payment plan established or may have the nominal fee waived, depending on circumstances. For patients who do not make payments at the time of service, statements are presented to them at the time of service and education is provided on additional elements such as payment plans, grace periods, and prompt payment incentives. Attempts are made to collect the discounted fees, but no patients are refused care as a result of non-payment. If a patient states they cannot pay, the patient meets with the Social Services Manager to better understand and overcome the patient's circumstances. If the patient cannot pay, FPCSN policy is that the fee will be waived. All patients are seen for the visit regardless of ability to pay.

[HEADING] BUDGET

[TEXT] Please see the FPCSN Budget Narrative attached to this application.

[HEADING] GOVERNANCE

[HEADING] Board Authority

[TEXT] The By-Laws for Family Practice & Counseling Services Network, Inc. are attached (Attachment 2). These By-Laws were developed this year and approved by the FPCSN Board on 4/16/25. The By-Laws indicate that the Board will meet Health Center Program requirements, including:

[HEADING] a. Monthly Meetings

[TEXT] The FPCSN By-Laws indicates in Article III Meetings that the Board is to meet at least once a month. Minutes are kept of all meetings and shared with Board members.

[HEADING] b. Approving and Evaluating the CEO

[TEXT] The By-Laws indicate in Article III Powers that the FPCSN Board is responsible for the selection and dismissal of the Chief Executive Officer.

[HEADING] c. Approving Annual Budget and Applications

[TEXT] The By-Laws indicate in Article III Powers that the FPCSN Board has the responsibility to approve the FPCSN project budget annually and to approve applications made for health center funding.

[HEADING] d. Approving Services Provided, Sites, and Hours of Operation

[TEXT] The By-Laws indicate in Article III Powers that the FPCSN Board has the responsibility to approve the services, locations, and hours of operation of the health center sites.

[HEADING] e. Evaluating Health Center Performance

[TEXT] The By-Laws indicate in Article III Powers that the FPCSN Board has the responsibility for evaluating the performance of the health center, including achievement of project objectives, service utilization patterns, quality of care, and efficiency and effectiveness.

[TEXT] f. Establishing Policy Related to Health Center Operations

[TEXT] The By-Laws indicate in Article III Powers that the FPCSN Board is responsible for establishing policy related to health center operations.

[TEXT] f/g. Establishes Policy Related to Health Center Operations and Assures Compliance The By-Laws indicate in Article III Powers that the FPCSN Board has the responsibility to assure that the health center operates in compliance with applicable federal, state, and local laws and regulations.

[HEADING] Full Board Authority and Oversight

[TEXT] The FPCSN Board elects its own members, as noted in Article III of the By-Laws. No individual, entity, or committee is noted as having authority or veto power over the Board and committees are specifically barred from amending the By-Laws or the Articles of Incorporation; selecting, approving, or dismissing Directors; or changing any resolution of the Board. There is no agreement or collaboration in place that restricts board authority.

[HEADING] Compliance with Health Center Program Board Composition Requirements

[TEXT] The Family Practice & Counseling Services Network Board is vested with full authority and responsibility for the operations of the health center. The By-Laws indicate in Article III that the FPCSN Board is to include between 9 and 15 members. In Article III Composition, the By-Laws indicate that at least 51% of members are to be patients of the health center and should include representation from public housing. Article III Composition also indicates that of the non-patient members no more than 50% may derive more than 10% of their income from the health care industry and they should be representative of the community, including public housing, and should have expertise in community affairs, government, finance, legal affairs, and other commercial and/or social services in the community. Article III Composition indicates that no Director may be an employee of FPCSN or an immediate family member (i.e., spouse, child, parent, or brother or sister through blood, adoption, or marriage) of such an employee.

[TEXT] There are currently twelve members on the FPCSN Board, six of whom are FPCSN patients. One member is a representative of the Housing Authority and two others are or have been public housing residents. As noted on the Board list, Form 6A, the FPSN Board members have expertise in a number of fields, including law, public relations, education, community engagement, and healthcare operations and strategy. Three of the six non-patient members derive income from the health care industry.

[TEXT] Describe, with specific examples, how you will use the requested federal funds to add new or expand existing services to the homeless population and/or residents of public housing within your service area, as well as how this is an increase or expansion of the services your organization was providing previously for these populations. (maximum 1,000 characters)

[TEXT] The health center has been providing health care services to residents of public housing and the surrounding communities in the service area for 33 years. Because the previous awardee changed ownership and relinquished the grant on 6/30/25, the FPCSN health center has established a new non-profit corporation and is applying as a new applicant for the area it has served for many years. In order to limit disruption in services to its patients, FPCSN has been able to keep all main sites open while providing the required services. However, in the last twelve months, because of the upheaval and uncertainty of the separation from the awardee and loss of FQHC status, many providers and other staff have left to seek positions elsewhere. Therefore, the requested federal funds will be used to add clinical provider staff to expand existing services so FPCSN can serve more patients with the service area.
